scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.michaelcaine.com">www<wbr />.michaelcaine<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Sir Michael Caine</b> <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:100%;"><a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born <b>Maurice Joseph Micklewhite</b>, 14 March 1933) is an English actor, producer, and author who has appeared in over 125 films and is considered to be a British film icon.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Known for his distinctive "<a href="/wiki/Cockney" title="Cockney">cockney</a>" accent, Caine was born in South London, where during his early childhood he and his parents lived in a rented flat on Urlwin Street, in <a href="/wiki/Camberwell" title="Camberwell">Camberwell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> about a mile-and-a-half south of the <a href="/wiki/Elephant_and_Castle" title="Elephant and Castle">Elephant and Castle</a>, the bustling London crossroads district referred to in the title of his most recent autobiography.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He made his breakthrough in the 1960s with starring roles in British films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Zulu_(1964_film)" title="Zulu (1964 film)">Zulu</a></i> (1964), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ipcress_File_(film)" title="The Ipcress File (film)">The Ipcress File</a></i> (1965), <i><a href="/wiki/Alfie_(1966_film)" title="Alfie (1966 film)">Alfie</a></i> (1966), for which he was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job" title="The Italian Job">The Italian Job</a></i> (1969), and <i><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain_(film)" title="Battle of Britain (film)">Battle of Britain</a></i> (1969). His roles in the 1970s included <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Carter" title="Get Carter">Get Carter</a></i> (1971), <a href="/wiki/The_Last_Valley_(1971_film)" title="The Last Valley (1971 film)"><i>The</i> <i>Last</i> <i>Valley</i></a> (1971), <i><a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(1972_film)" title="Sleuth (1972 film)">Sleuth</a></i> (1972), for which he earned his second Academy Award nomination, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Would_Be_King_(film)" title="The Man Who Would Be King (film)">The Man Who Would Be King</a></i> (1975), and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bridge_Too_Far_(film)" title="A Bridge Too Far (film)">A Bridge Too Far</a></i> (1977). He achieved some of his greatest critical success in the 1980s, with <i><a href="/wiki/Educating_Rita_(film)" title="Educating Rita (film)">Educating Rita</a></i> (1983), earning him the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actor_in_a_Leading_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actor in a Leading Role">BAFTA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor \xe2\x80\x93 Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe Award for Best Actor</a>. In 1986, he received an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor</a> for his performance in <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Hannah_and_Her_Sisters" title="Hannah and Her Sisters">Hannah and Her Sisters</a></i>.\n</p><p>Caine played <a href="/wiki/Ebenezer_Scrooge" title="Ebenezer Scrooge">Ebenezer Scrooge</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Muppet_Christmas_Carol" title="The Muppet Christmas Carol">The Muppet Christmas Carol</a></i> (1992). This was his first starring role in several years, which led to a career resurgence in the late 1990s, receiving his second Golden Globe Award for his performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Voice_(film)" title="Little Voice (film)">Little Voice</a></i> in 1998, and receiving his second Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cider_House_Rules_(film)" title="The Cider House Rules (film)">The Cider House Rules</a></i> the following year. Caine played <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Powers" title="Nigel Powers">Nigel Powers</a> in the 2002 parody <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers_in_Goldmember" title="Austin Powers in Goldmember">Austin Powers in Goldmember</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a> in <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Trilogy" class="mw-redirect" title="The Dark Knight Trilogy">The Dark Knight Trilogy</a></i>. He appeared in several other of Nolan\'s films, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prestige_(film)" title="The Prestige (film)">The Prestige</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> (2010), and <i><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">Interstellar</a></i> (2014). He also appeared in <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n">Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_Men" title="Children of Men">Children of Men</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Vaughn" title="Matthew Vaughn">Matthew Vaughn</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Action_comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Action comedy">action comedy</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Kingsman:_The_Secret_Service" title="Kingsman: The Secret Service">Kingsman: The Secret Service</a></i>. As of February 2017, films in which he has starred have grossed over $3.5 billion domestically, and over $7.8 billion worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Caine is ranked as the twelfth-highest-grossing box office star.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine is one of only two actors nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> for acting in every decade from the 1960s to the 2000s (the other one being <a href="/wiki/Jack_Nicholson" title="Jack Nicholson">Jack Nicholson</a>; <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Laurence Olivier</a> was also nominated for an acting Academy Award in five different decades, beginning in 1939 and ending in 1978). Caine appeared in seven films that featured in the <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/BFI_Top_100_British_films" title="BFI Top 100 British films">100 greatest British films of the 20th century</a>. In 2000, Caine received a <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Fellowship" title="BAFTA Fellowship">BAFTA Fellowship</a>, and was <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of the United Kingdom">knighted</a> by Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> in recognition of his contribution to cinema.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Military_career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Military career</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Acting_career"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Acting career</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#1950s"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">1950s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#1960s"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">1960s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#1970s"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">1970s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#1980s"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">1980s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#1990s"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">1990s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#2000s"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">2000s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#2010s"><span class="tocnumber">3.7</span> <span class="toctext">2010s</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Popular_culture"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Popular culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Political_views"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Political views</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Music_interests"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Music interests</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Filmography"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Filmography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Awards_and_honours"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and honours</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg/220px-Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg/330px-Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg/440px-Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="420" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Michael_Caine_Plaque_-_geograph.org.uk_-_497396.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Blue_plaque" title="Blue plaque">blue plaque</a> erected in 2003 marks Caine\'s birthplace at St Olave\'s Hospital</div></div></div>\n<p>Michael Caine was born Maurice Joseph Micklewhite on 14 March 1933 in <a href="/wiki/St_Olave%27s_Hospital" title="St Olave&#39;s Hospital">St Olave\'s Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rotherhithe" title="Rotherhithe">Rotherhithe</a>, London.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1965_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1965-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His father, Maurice Joseph Micklewhite Sr., was a <a href="/wiki/Fish_market" title="Fish market">fish market</a> porter, while his mother, Ellen Frances Marie Burchell, was a cook and <a href="/wiki/Charwoman" title="Charwoman">charwoman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FilmRefbio_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmRefbio-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His father had <a href="/wiki/Irish_Traveller" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Traveller">Irish Traveller</a> ancestry,<sup id="cite_ref-bravo_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bravo-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and was a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, though the actor was brought up in his mother\'s <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> religion.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine had an elder maternal half-brother named David William Burchell, and a younger full brother, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Caine" title="Stanley Caine">Stanley Micklewhite</a>. He grew up in <a href="/wiki/Southwark" title="Southwark">Southwark</a>, London, and during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, he was <a href="/wiki/Evacuations_of_civilians_in_Britain_during_World_War_II" title="Evacuations of civilians in Britain during World War II">evacuated</a> to <a href="/wiki/North_Runcton" title="North Runcton">North Runcton</a> near <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn" title="King&#39;s Lynn">King\'s Lynn</a> in Norfolk.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> After the war, his father was <a href="/wiki/Demobilization" title="Demobilization">demobilised</a>, and the family were rehoused by the council in Marshall Gardens at the <a href="/wiki/Elephant_and_Castle" title="Elephant and Castle">Elephant and Castle</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Prefabricated_home" title="Prefabricated home">prefabricated house</a> made in Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> as much of London\'s housing stock had been damaged during <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a> in 1940\xe2\x80\x931941:\n</p>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The prefabs, as they were known, were intended to be temporary homes while London was reconstructed, but we ended up living there for eighteen years and for us, after a cramped flat with an outside toilet, it was luxury.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n<p>In 1944, he passed his <a href="/wiki/Eleven-plus" title="Eleven-plus">eleven-plus</a> exam, winning a scholarship to <a href="/wiki/Hackney_Downs_School" title="Hackney Downs School">Hackney Downs School</a> (formerly The Grocers\' Company\'s School).<sup id="cite_ref-Micklewhite_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Micklewhite-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After a year there he moved to Wilson\'s Grammar School in Camberwell (now <a href="/wiki/Wilson%27s_School" title="Wilson&#39;s School">Wilson\'s School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wallington,_London" title="Wallington, London">Wallington, London</a>), which he left at sixteen after gaining a <a href="/wiki/School_Certificate_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="School Certificate (UK)">School Certificate</a> in six subjects. He then worked briefly as a filing clerk and messenger for a film company in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_London" title="Victoria, London">Victoria Street</a> and film producer <a href="/wiki/Jay_Lewis" title="Jay Lewis">Jay Lewis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wardour_Street" title="Wardour Street">Wardour Street</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70notout_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70notout-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_career">Military career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Military career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>From 28 April 1952, when he was <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Conscription in the United Kingdom">called up</a> to do his <a href="/wiki/National_service" title="National service">national service</a> until 1954, he served in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fusiliers" title="Royal Fusiliers">Royal Fusiliers</a>, first at the <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">BAOR</a> HQ in <a href="/wiki/Iserlohn" title="Iserlohn">Iserlohn</a>, Germany, and then on active service during the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>. He had gone into Korea feeling sympathetic to <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a>, coming as he did from a poor family, but the experience left him permanently repelled.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He experienced a situation where he knew he was going to die, the memory of which stayed with him and formed his character; he later said, "The rest of my life I have lived every bloody moment from the moment I wake up until the time I go to sleep."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He detailed the incident in his autobiography, "The Elephant to Hollywood"<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-Elephant_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elephant-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine would like to see the return of national service to help combat <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">youth violence</a>, stating: "I\'m just saying, put them in the Army for six months. You\'re there to learn how to defend your country. You belong to the country. Then, when you come out, you have a sense of belonging, rather than a sense of violence."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">Acting career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Acting career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s">1950s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1950s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Caine began his acting career at the age of 20 in <a href="/wiki/Horsham" title="Horsham">Horsham, Sussex</a>, when he responded to an advertisement in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Stage" title="The Stage">The Stage</a></i> for an assistant stage manager who would also perform small <a href="/wiki/Bit_part" title="Bit part">walk-on parts</a> for the Horsham-based Westminster Repertory Company who were performing at the <a href="/wiki/Horsham#Town_centre" title="Horsham">Carfax</a> Electric Theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Adopting the stage name "Michael White", in July 1953 he was cast as the drunkard Hindley in the Company\'s production of <i><a href="/wiki/Wuthering_Heights" title="Wuthering Heights">Wuthering Heights</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> He moved to the <a href="/wiki/Lowestoft" title="Lowestoft">Lowestoft</a> Repertory Company in <a href="/wiki/Suffolk" title="Suffolk">Suffolk</a> for a year when he was 21. It was here that he met his first wife.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He has described the first nine years of his career as "really, really brutal."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Whilst in Lowestoft rep at the Arcadia Theatre (with Jackson Stanley\'s \'Standard Players\') he appeared in nine plays.\n</p><p>When his career took him to London in 1954 after his provincial apprenticeship, his agent informed him that there was already a Michael White performing as an actor in London and that he had to come up with a new name immediately. Speaking to his agent from a <a href="/wiki/Telephone_booth" title="Telephone booth">telephone booth</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Square" title="Leicester Square">Leicester Square</a>, London, he looked around for inspiration, noted that <i><a href="/wiki/The_Caine_Mutiny_(film)" title="The Caine Mutiny (film)">The Caine Mutiny</a></i> was being shown at the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Odeon Cinema">Odeon Cinema</a> in 1954, and decided to change his name to "Michael Caine". He joked on television in 1987 that, had a tree partly blocking his view been a few feet to the left, he might have been called "Michael Mutiny". (<a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Bogart" title="Humphrey Bogart">Humphrey Bogart</a> was his "screen idol" and he would later play the part originally intended for Bogart in <a href="/wiki/John_Huston" title="John Huston">John Huston</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Would_Be_King_(film)" title="The Man Who Would Be King (film)">The Man Who Would Be King</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>) He also later joked in interviews that had he looked the other way, he would have ended up as "Michael <a href="/wiki/One_Hundred_and_One_Dalmatians" title="One Hundred and One Dalmatians">One Hundred and One Dalmatians</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In 1959, he was <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Toole" title="Peter O&#39;Toole">Peter O\'Toole</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Understudy" title="Understudy">understudy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Anderson" title="Lindsay Anderson">Lindsay Anderson</a>\'s West End staging of <a href="/wiki/Willis_Hall" title="Willis Hall">Willis Hall</a>\'s <i>The Long and the Short and the Tall</i>. He took over the role when O\'Toole left to make <i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawrence of Arabia">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i> and went on to a four-month tour of Britain and Ireland.\n</p><p>Michael Caine\'s first film role was as one of the privates in <a href="/wiki/George_Baker_(actor)" title="George Baker (actor)">George Baker</a>\'s platoon in the 1956 film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hill_in_Korea" title="A Hill in Korea">A Hill in Korea</a></i>. The stars of the film were <a href="/wiki/George_Baker_(actor)" title="George Baker (actor)">George Baker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baker" title="Stanley Baker">Stanley Baker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Andrews" title="Harry Andrews">Harry Andrews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Medwin" title="Michael Medwin">Michael Medwin</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Boyd" title="Stephen Boyd">Stephen Boyd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Lewis_(actor)" title="Ronald Lewis (actor)">Ronald Lewis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Shaw_(actor)" title="Robert Shaw (actor)">Robert Shaw</a> also had a small part.\n</p><p>He appeared regularly on television in small roles. His first credited role on the BBC was \'Boudousse\' in the <a href="/wiki/Jean_Anouilh" title="Jean Anouilh">Jean Anouilh</a> play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lark_(play)" title="The Lark (play)">The Lark</a></i> in 1956. Other parts included three roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Dixon_of_Dock_Green" title="Dixon of Dock Green">Dixon of Dock Green</a></i> in 1957, 1958 and 1959, prisoner-of-war series <i><a href="/wiki/Escape_(UK_TV_series)" title="Escape (UK TV series)">Escape</a></i> (1957), crime/thriller drama <i>Mister Charlesworth</i>, and a court orderly in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Caine_Mutiny_Court-Martial" title="The Caine Mutiny Court-Martial">The Caine Mutiny Court-Martial</a></i> (1958).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael-caine-trailer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Michael-caine-trailer.jpg/240px-Michael-caine-trailer.jpg" width="240" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Michael-caine-trailer.jpg/360px-Michael-caine-trailer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Michael-caine-trailer.jpg/480px-Michael-caine-trailer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1605" data-file-height="693" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael-caine-trailer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Michael Caine in the trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/Zulu_(1964_film)" title="Zulu (1964 film)">Zulu</a></i> (1964)</div></div></div>\n<p>Caine continued to appear on television, in serials <i>The Golden Girl</i> and <i>No Wreath for the General</i>, but was then cast in the play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Compartment" title="The Compartment">The Compartment</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Speight" title="Johnny Speight">Johnny Speight</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Two-hander" title="Two-hander">two-hander</a> also starring <a href="/wiki/Frank_Finlay" title="Frank Finlay">Frank Finlay</a>. This was followed by main roles in other plays including the character Tosh in <i>Somewhere for the Night</i>, a <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_Sunday-Night_Play" title="BBC Sunday-Night Play">Sunday-Night Play</a></i> written by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Naughton" title="Bill Naughton">Bill Naughton</a> televised on Sunday 3 December 1961, another two-hander by Johnny Speight, <i>The Playmates</i>, and two editions of BBC plays strand <i><a href="/wiki/First_Night" title="First Night">First Night</a></i>, <i>Funny Noises with Their Mouths</i> and <i>The Way with Reggie</i> (both 1963). He also acted in radio plays, including Bill Naughton\'s <i>Looking for Frankie</i> on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Home_Service" title="BBC Home Service">BBC Home Service</a> (1963) and <i><a href="/wiki/Ping_Pong" class="mw-redirect" title="Ping Pong">Ping Pong</a></i> on the BBC Third Programme (1964).\nA big break came for Caine when he was cast as Meff in James Saunders\' <a href="/wiki/Cockney" title="Cockney">Cockney</a> comedy <i>Next Time I\'ll Sing To You</i>, when this play was presented at the <a href="/wiki/Arts_Theatre" title="Arts Theatre">New Arts Theatre</a> in London on 23 January 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Scenes from the play\'s performance were featured in the April 1963 issue of <i>Theatre World</i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When this play moved to the <a href="/wiki/Criterion_Theatre" title="Criterion Theatre">Criterion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly" title="Piccadilly">Piccadilly</a> with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Codron" title="Michael Codron">Michael Codron</a> directing, he was visited backstage by <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baker" title="Stanley Baker">Stanley Baker</a>, one of the four stars in Caine\'s first film, <i>A Hill in Korea</i>, who told him about the part of a Cockney private in his upcoming film <i><a href="/wiki/Zulu_(1964_film)" title="Zulu (1964 film)">Zulu</a></i>, a film Baker was producing and starring in. Baker told Caine to meet the director, <a href="/wiki/Cy_Endfield" title="Cy Endfield">Cy Endfield</a>, who informed him that he already had given the part to <a href="/wiki/James_Booth" title="James Booth">James Booth</a>, a fellow Cockney who was Caine\'s friend, because he "looked more Cockney" than Caine did. Endfield then told the 6\'2" Caine that he did not look like a Cockney but like an officer, and offered him a screen test for the role of a snobbish, upper class officer after Caine assured him that he could do a <a href="/wiki/Posh_accent" class="mw-redirect" title="Posh accent">posh accent</a>. Caine believes Endfield offered him, a Cockney, the role of an aristocrat because, being American, he did not have the endemic British class-prejudice. Though he tested poorly, Endfield gave him the part that would make him a film star.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Location shooting for <i>Zulu</i> took place in <a href="/wiki/Natal_(Province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Natal (Province)">Natal</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, for 14 weeks in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> According to his 2011 autobiography <i>The Elephant to Hollywood</i>, Caine had been signed to a seven-year contract by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Levine" title="Joseph E. Levine">Joseph E. Levine</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Embassy_Pictures" title="Embassy Pictures">Embassy Films</a> was distributing <i>Zulu</i>. After the return of the cast to England and the completion of the film, Levine released him from the contract, telling him, "I know you\'re not, but you gotta face the fact that you look like a queer on screen." Levine gave his contract to his <i>Zulu</i> co-star James Booth.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_La_Warr_Pavilion,_28_August_2012_(6).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/De_La_Warr_Pavilion%2C_28_August_2012_%286%29.jpg/220px-De_La_Warr_Pavilion%2C_28_August_2012_%286%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/De_La_Warr_Pavilion%2C_28_August_2012_%286%29.jpg/330px-De_La_Warr_Pavilion%2C_28_August_2012_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/De_La_Warr_Pavilion%2C_28_August_2012_%286%29.jpg/440px-De_La_Warr_Pavilion%2C_28_August_2012_%286%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="3056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_La_Warr_Pavilion,_28_August_2012_(6).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The artwork <i>Hang On A Minute Lads, I\'ve Got A Great Idea</i>, the famous line by Caine at the end of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job" title="The Italian Job">The Italian Job</a></i> (1969), by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wilson_(sculptor)" title="Richard Wilson (sculptor)">Richard Wilson</a> on the <a href="/wiki/De_La_Warr_Pavilion" title="De La Warr Pavilion">De La Warr Pavilion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bexhill-on-Sea" title="Bexhill-on-Sea">Bexhill-on-Sea</a>, England</div></div></div>\n<p>Subsequently, Caine\'s agent got him cast in the BBC production <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet_at_Elsinore" title="Hamlet at Elsinore">Hamlet at Elsinore</a></i> (1964) as <a href="/wiki/Horatio_(character)" class="mw-redirect" title="Horatio (character)">Horatio</a>, in support of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Plummer" title="Christopher Plummer">Christopher Plummer</a>\'s Hamlet. Horatio was the only classical role which Caine, who had never received dramatic training, would ever play. Caine wrote, "...I decided that if my on-screen appearance was going to be an issue, then I would use it to bring out all Horatio\'s ambiguous sexuality."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine\'s roles as effete-seeming aristocrats were to contrast with his next projects, in which he was to become notable for using a <a href="/wiki/Regional_accents_of_English" title="Regional accents of English">regional accent</a>, rather than the <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">Received Pronunciation</a> then considered proper for film actors. At the time, Caine\'s working class <a href="/wiki/Cockney" title="Cockney">Cockney</a>, just as with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Liverpudlian" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpudlian">Liverpudlian</a> accents, stood out to American and British audiences alike. <i>Zulu</i> was closely followed by two of his best-known roles: the spy <a href="/wiki/Harry_Palmer" title="Harry Palmer">Harry Palmer</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ipcress_File_(film)" title="The Ipcress File (film)">The Ipcress File</a></i> (1965), and the womanising title character in <i><a href="/wiki/Alfie_(1966_film)" title="Alfie (1966 film)">Alfie</a></i> (1966). He went on to play Palmer in a further four films, <i><a href="/wiki/Funeral_in_Berlin_(film)" title="Funeral in Berlin (film)">Funeral in Berlin</a></i> (1966), <i><a href="/wiki/Billion_Dollar_Brain" title="Billion Dollar Brain">Billion Dollar Brain</a></i> (1967), <i><a href="/wiki/Bullet_to_Beijing" title="Bullet to Beijing">Bullet to Beijing</a></i> (1995) and <i><a href="/wiki/Midnight_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Midnight in Saint Petersburg">Midnight in Saint Petersburg</a></i> (1995). Caine made his first film in Hollywood in 1966, after an invitation from <a href="/wiki/Shirley_MacLaine" title="Shirley MacLaine">Shirley MacLaine</a> to play opposite her in <i><a href="/wiki/Gambit_(1966_film)" title="Gambit (1966 film)">Gambit</a>.</i> During the first two weeks, whilst staying at <a href="/wiki/The_Beverly_Hills_Hotel" title="The Beverly Hills Hotel">the Beverly Hills Hotel</a>, he met long-term friends <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne" title="John Wayne">John Wayne</a> and agent <a href="/wiki/Irving_Paul_Lazar" title="Irving Paul Lazar">"Swifty" Lazar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Caine starred in the 1969 comedy <a href="/wiki/Caper_story" title="Caper story">caper film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job" title="The Italian Job">The Italian Job</a></i> as the leader of a cockney criminal gang released from prison with the intention of doing a "big job" in Italy to steal gold bullion from an armoured security truck. The line "You\'re only supposed to blow the bloody doors off!" by Caine was voted favourite film one-liner in a 2003 poll of 1,000 film fans.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Get-carter-trailer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Get-carter-trailer.jpg/240px-Get-carter-trailer.jpg" width="240" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Get-carter-trailer.jpg/360px-Get-carter-trailer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Get-carter-trailer.jpg/480px-Get-carter-trailer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Get-carter-trailer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Michael Caine in the trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Carter" title="Get Carter">Get Carter</a></i> (1971)</div></div></div>\n<p>After working on <i>The Italian Job</i> with <a href="/wiki/No%C3%ABl_Coward" title="No\xc3\xabl Coward">No\xc3\xabl Coward</a>, and a solid role as <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> fighter pilot <a href="/wiki/Squadron_leader" title="Squadron leader">squadron leader</a> Canfield in the all-star cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain_(film)" title="Battle of Britain (film)">Battle of Britain</a></i> (both 1969), Caine played the lead in <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Carter" title="Get Carter">Get Carter</a></i> (1971), a British gangster film. Caine was busy with successes including <i><a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(1972_film)" title="Sleuth (1972 film)">Sleuth</a></i> (1972) opposite <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Laurence Olivier</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Huston" title="John Huston">John Huston</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Would_Be_King_(film)" title="The Man Who Would Be King (film)">The Man Who Would Be King</a></i> (1975) co-starring <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> which received widespread acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-king_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> applauded the "lovely double act of Caine and Connery, clowning to their doom", while Huston paid tribute to Caine\'s improvisation as an actor: "Michael is one of the most intelligent men among the artists I\'ve known. I don\'t particularly care to throw the ball to an actor and let him improvise, but with Michael it\'s different. I just let him get on with it."<sup id="cite_ref-king_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1976 he appeared in the screen adaptation by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Mankiewicz" title="Tom Mankiewicz">Tom Mankiewicz</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Jack_Higgins" title="Jack Higgins">Jack Higgins</a> novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Eagle_Has_Landed_(film)" title="The Eagle Has Landed (film)">The Eagle Has Landed</a></i> as <i><a href="/wiki/Oberst" title="Oberst">Oberst</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Colonel" title="Colonel">Colonel</a>) Kurt Steiner, the commander of a <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> paratroop unit disguised as Polish <a href="/wiki/Paratrooper" title="Paratrooper">paratroopers</a>, whose mission was to kidnap or kill the then-<a href="/wiki/British_Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="British Prime Minister">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, alongside co-stars <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sutherland" title="Donald Sutherland">Donald Sutherland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Duvall" title="Robert Duvall">Robert Duvall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Agutter" title="Jenny Agutter">Jenny Agutter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donald_Pleasence" title="Donald Pleasence">Donald Pleasence</a>. Subsequently, in 1978, he starred in <a href="/wiki/Silver_Bears_(film)" title="Silver Bears (film)"><i>The Silver Bears</i></a>, an adaptation of Paul Erdman\'s (1974) novel of the same name. Caine also was part of an all-star cast in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bridge_Too_Far_(film)" title="A Bridge Too Far (film)">A Bridge Too Far</a></i> (1977).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg/170px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg/255px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg/340px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Michael_Caine_in_%27Ashanti%27.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caine in 1979</div></div></div>\n<p>At the end of the 1970s Caine\'s choice of roles was frequently criticised\xe2\x80\x94something to which he has referred with self-deprecating comments about taking parts strictly for the money. Caine then averaged two films a year, but these included such failures as the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA</a>-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magus_(film)" title="The Magus (film)">The Magus</a></i> (1968), the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a>-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/The_Swarm_(film)" title="The Swarm (film)">The Swarm</a></i> (1978), <i><a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(1979_film)" title="Ashanti (1979 film)">Ashanti</a></i> (1979) (which he claimed were his worst three films), <i><a href="/wiki/Beyond_the_Poseidon_Adventure" title="Beyond the Poseidon Adventure">Beyond the Poseidon Adventure</a></i> (1979), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Island_(1980_film)" title="The Island (1980 film)">The Island</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hand_(1981_film)" title="The Hand (1981 film)">The Hand</a></i> (1981) and a reunion with his <i><a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(1972_film)" title="Sleuth (1972 film)">Sleuth</a></i> co-star <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Laurence Olivier</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jigsaw_Man_(film)" title="The Jigsaw Man (film)">The Jigsaw Man</a></i> (1982).\n</p><p>Caine\'s acclaimed roles during the 1980s included a <a href="/wiki/BAFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA">BAFTA</a>-winning turn in <i><a href="/wiki/Educating_Rita_(film)" title="Educating Rita (film)">Educating Rita</a></i> (1983) in which he co-starred with <a href="/wiki/Julie_Walters" title="Julie Walters">Julie Walters</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a>-winning performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Hannah_and_Her_Sisters" title="Hannah and Her Sisters">Hannah and Her Sisters</a></i> (1986), and a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a>-nominated one in <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Rotten_Scoundrels_(film)" title="Dirty Rotten Scoundrels (film)">Dirty Rotten Scoundrels</a></i> (1988) co-starring <a href="/wiki/Steve_Martin" title="Steve Martin">Steve Martin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> He continued to appear in poorly received films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Blame_It_on_Rio" title="Blame It on Rio">Blame It on Rio</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clement" title="Dick Clement">Dick Clement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ian_La_Frenais" title="Ian La Frenais">Ian La Frenais</a> comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Water_(1985_film)" title="Water (1985 film)">Water</a></i>, the critical-commercial flop <i><a href="/wiki/Jaws:_The_Revenge" title="Jaws: The Revenge">Jaws: The Revenge</a></i> (1987) (about which he had mixed feelings concerning the production and the final cut), and <i><a href="/wiki/Bullseye!_(1990_film)" title="Bullseye! (1990 film)">Bullseye!</a></i> (1990). On <i>Jaws: The Revenge</i>, Caine said "I have never seen the film, but by all accounts it was terrible. However, I have seen the house that it built, and it is terrific."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>His other successful films (critically or financially) were the 1978 Academy Award-winning <i><a href="/wiki/California_Suite_(film)" title="California Suite (film)">California Suite</a></i>, the 1980 Golden Globe-nominated <a href="/wiki/Slasher_film" title="Slasher film">slasher film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Dressed_to_Kill_(1980_film)" title="Dressed to Kill (1980 film)">Dressed to Kill</a></i>, the 1981 <a href="/wiki/War_film" title="War film">war film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Escape_to_Victory" title="Escape to Victory">Escape to Victory</a></i> featuring <a href="/wiki/Sylvester_Stallone" title="Sylvester Stallone">Sylvester Stallone</a> and footballers from the 1960s and 1970s, including <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pel\xc3\xa9">Pel\xc3\xa9</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Moore" title="Bobby Moore">Bobby Moore</a>, the 1982 film <i><a href="/wiki/Deathtrap_(film)" title="Deathtrap (film)">Deathtrap</a></i>, and the 1986 Academy Award-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/Mona_Lisa_(film)" title="Mona Lisa (film)">Mona Lisa</a></i>. In 1987, Caine narrated <i><a href="/wiki/Hero_(1987_film)" title="Hero (1987 film)">Hero</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_official_FIFA_World_Cup_films" class="mw-redirect" title="List of official FIFA World Cup films">official film</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He also starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Without_a_Clue" title="Without a Clue">Without a Clue</a></i>, portraying <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">Sherlock Holmes</a> and also acted as Chief Insp. Frederick Abberline in the 1988 TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Ripper_(1988_TV_series)" title="Jack the Ripper (1988 TV series)">Jack the Ripper</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 1990s, Caine found good parts harder to come by. He played the mysterious bartender Mike in <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Destiny" title="Mr. Destiny">Mr. Destiny</a></i> in 1990. A high point came when he played <a href="/wiki/Ebenezer_Scrooge" title="Ebenezer Scrooge">Ebenezer Scrooge</a> in the critically acclaimed <i><a href="/wiki/The_Muppet_Christmas_Carol" title="The Muppet Christmas Carol">The Muppet Christmas Carol</a></i> (1992). He played the beleaguered stage director Lloyd Fellowes in the film adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Noises_Off_(film)" title="Noises Off (film)">Noises Off</a></i> (1992). He also played a villain in the <a href="/wiki/Steven_Seagal" title="Steven Seagal">Steven Seagal</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/On_Deadly_Ground" title="On Deadly Ground">On Deadly Ground</a></i> (1994). He was in two <a href="/wiki/Straight_to_video" class="mw-redirect" title="Straight to video">straight to video</a> Harry Palmer sequels and a few television films. However, Caine\'s reputation as a pop icon was still intact, thanks to his roles in films such as <i>The Italian Job</i> and <i>Get Carter</i>. His performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Voice_(film)" title="Little Voice (film)">Little Voice</a></i> (1998) was seen as something of a return to form, and won him a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a>. Better parts followed, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cider_House_Rules_(film)" title="The Cider House Rules (film)">The Cider House Rules</a></i> (1999), for which he won his second <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg/200px-The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg" width="200" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg/300px-The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg/400px-The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="914" data-file-height="1364" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Dark_Knight_European_Premiere_-_Michael_Caine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caine in London at the European premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>, July 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 2000s, Caine appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Miss_Congeniality_(film)" title="Miss Congeniality (film)">Miss Congeniality</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/Last_Orders_(film)" title="Last Orders (film)">Last Orders</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Quiet_American_(2002_film)" title="The Quiet American (2002 film)">The Quiet American</a></i> (2002), for which he was Oscar-nominated, and others. Several of Caine\'s classic films have been remade, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job" title="The Italian Job">The Italian Job</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Carter" title="Get Carter">Get Carter</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alfie_(1966_film)" title="Alfie (1966 film)">Alfie</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(1972_film)" title="Sleuth (1972 film)">Sleuth</a></i>. In the <a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(2007_film)" title="Sleuth (2007 film)">2007 remake</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(1972_film)" title="Sleuth (1972 film)">Sleuth</a></i>, Caine took over the role <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Laurence Olivier</a> played in the <a href="/wiki/Sleuth_(1972_film)" title="Sleuth (1972 film)">1972 version</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jude_Law" title="Jude Law">Jude Law</a> played Caine\'s original role. Caine is one of the few actors to have played a starring role in two different versions of the same film. In an interview with CNN, Law spoke of his admiration for Caine: "I learned so much just from watching how he monitored his performance, and also how little he has to do. He\'s a master technician and sometimes he was doing stuff I didn\'t see, I couldn\'t register. I\'d go back and watch it on the monitor, it was like \'Oh my God, the amount of variety he\'s put in there is breathtaking".<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine also starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers_in_Goldmember" title="Austin Powers in Goldmember">Austin Powers in Goldmember</a></i> (2002) as Austin\'s father and in 2003 he co-starred with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Duvall" title="Robert Duvall">Robert Duvall</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Secondhand_Lions" title="Secondhand Lions">Secondhand Lions</a></i>. Caine played family elder Henry Lair in the 2004 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Around_the_Bend" title="Around the Bend">Around the Bend</a></i>. In 2005, he was cast as <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Wayne" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruce Wayne">Bruce Wayne</a>\'s butler <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a> in the first production of the new <a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins"><i>Batman</i> film series</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i>. Also in 2005, he played as Isabel\'s (Nicole Kidman) father in Bewitched. In 2006, he appeared in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_Men" title="Children of Men">Children of Men</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prestige_(film)" title="The Prestige (film)">The Prestige</a></i>. In 2007 he appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Flawless_(2007_film)" title="Flawless (2007 film)">Flawless</a></i>, and in 2008 and 2012 he reprised his role as Alfred in <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>\'s critically acclaimed <i>Batman</i> sequels, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i> as well as starring in the British drama <i><a href="/wiki/Is_Anybody_There%3F" title="Is Anybody There?">Is Anybody There?</a></i>, which explores the final days of life.\n</p><p>It was reported by <a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)"><i>Empire</i></a> magazine that Caine had said that <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Brown_(film)" title="Harry Brown (film)">Harry Brown</a></i> (released on 13 November 2009) would be his last lead role.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Caine later clarified that he had no intention of retiring, stating that "You don\xe2\x80\x99t retire in this business, the business retires you."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/220px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/330px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/440px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1004" data-file-height="546" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caine (second from right) with the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> at the 10 July premiere in 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>Caine appeared in Christopher Nolan\'s science fiction thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> as Prof. Stephen Miles, Cobb\'s (<a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>) mentor and father-in-law. He voiced Finn McMissile in <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>\'s 2011 film <i><a href="/wiki/Cars_2" title="Cars 2">Cars 2</a></i> and also voiced a supporting role in the animation, <i><a href="/wiki/Gnomeo_%26_Juliet" title="Gnomeo &amp; Juliet">Gnomeo &amp; Juliet</a></i>. He also starred in the 2012 film <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_2:_The_Mysterious_Island" title="Journey 2: The Mysterious Island">Journey 2: The Mysterious Island</a></i>, as <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hutcherson" title="Josh Hutcherson">Josh Hutcherson</a>\'s character\'s grandfather; the film also featured <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Johnson" title="Dwayne Johnson">Dwayne Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Hudgens" title="Vanessa Hudgens">Vanessa Hudgens</a>.\n</p><p>Caine reprised his role as Alfred Pennyworth in the Batman sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>, which was released in July 2012. He appeared in Christopher Nolan\'s 2014 science-fiction film, <i><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">Interstellar</a></i> as Dr. Brand.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Caine co-starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Kingsman:_The_Secret_Service" title="Kingsman: The Secret Service">Kingsman: The Secret Service</a></i> (2014), by director <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Vaughn" title="Matthew Vaughn">Matthew Vaughn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He also appeared in the lead role of retired composer Fred Ballinger in the comedy-drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Youth_(2015_film)" title="Youth (2015 film)">Youth</a></i>, for which he received widespread acclaim.\n</p><p>In October 2015, Caine read <a href="/wiki/Hans_Christian_Andersen" title="Hans Christian Andersen">Hans Christian Andersen</a>\'s "Little Claus and Big Claus" for the children\'s fairytales app GivingTales in aid of <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/Roger_Moore" title="Roger Moore">Sir Roger Moore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ewan_McGregor" title="Ewan McGregor">Ewan McGregor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Collins" title="Joan Collins">Dame Joan Collins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Lumley" title="Joanna Lumley">Joanna Lumley</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Walliams" title="David Walliams">David Walliams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Rampling" title="Charlotte Rampling">Charlotte Rampling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_McKenna" title="Paul McKenna">Paul McKenna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Caine was cast in a spoken <a href="/wiki/Cameo_role" class="mw-redirect" title="Cameo role">cameo role</a> in Christopher Nolan\'s 2017 action-thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_(2017_film)" title="Dunkirk (2017 film)">Dunkirk</a></i> (2017), based on the <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation" title="Dunkirk evacuation">Dunkirk evacuation</a> of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, as a Royal Air Force Spitfire pilot, as a nod to his role in <i><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain_(film)" title="Battle of Britain (film)">Battle of Britain</a></i> (1969).<sup id="cite_ref-Whitty-2017_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whitty-2017-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Faber&amp;Faber-2017_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faber&amp;Faber-2017-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"I kept my cockney accent in order to let other working class boys know that if I made it, they could do it too."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Caine speaking to CNN\'s <i>The Screening Room</i> in 2007 on retaining his accent.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Caine is regarded as a <a href="/wiki/British_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="British culture">British cultural icon</a>, with Mairi Mackay of CNN stating: "Michael Caine has been personifying British cool since the swinging sixties. He has brought some of British cinema\'s most iconic characters to life and introduced his very own laid-back <a href="/wiki/Cockney" title="Cockney">cockney</a> gangster into pop culture. He doggedly retained a regional accent at a time when the plummy tones of <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">Received Pronunciation</a> were considered obligatory. It is a sweet irony that his accent has become his calling card."<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> With his distinctive voice and manner of speaking, Caine is a popular subject for impersonators and mimics.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Most Caine impressions include the catchphrase "Not a lot of people know that."<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The catchphrase emanates from Caine\'s habit of informing people of obscure "interesting facts" that he has collected.<sup id="cite_ref-Caine_facts_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caine_facts-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Referring to Caine as being the "biggest mine of useless information", <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a> initiated the catchphrase when he appeared on BBC1\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Michael_Parkinson" title="Michael Parkinson">Parkinson</a></i> show on 28 October 1972 and said:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Not many people know that. This is my Michael Caine impression. You see, Mike\'s always quoting from the <i>Guinness Book of Records</i>. At the drop of a hat he\'ll trot one out. \'Did you know that it takes a man in a tweed suit five-and-a-half seconds to fall from the top of <a href="/wiki/Big_Ben" title="Big Ben">Big Ben</a> to the ground?\' Now there\'s not many people who know that!<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Over the years Caine himself had parodied the phenomenon, both his catchphrase and his "interesting facts", and has imitated others\' impressions of him.<sup id="cite_ref-huffingtonpost.com_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Parkinson" title="Michael Parkinson">Michael Parkinson</a> in 2007, Caine commented on the impersonations of his voice, "I can do it. \'Hello. My name is Michael Caine. Not many people know that.\' I sound like a bloody moron. You know where they\'ve got me now? On birthday cards. \'It\'s your birthday today. Not many people know that\'. Now they\'ve got me on Satellite navigation. It\'s me going, \'take the second turn on the right, and you\'ll wind up right in the shit.\'"<sup id="cite_ref-huffingtonpost.com_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In 1983, Caine used his "not a lot of people know that" phrase as a joke in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Educating_Rita_(film)" title="Educating Rita (film)">Educating Rita</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mme_Tussaud_museum_(2848368706).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Mme_Tussaud_museum_%282848368706%29.jpg/220px-Mme_Tussaud_museum_%282848368706%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Mme_Tussaud_museum_%282848368706%29.jpg/330px-Mme_Tussaud_museum_%282848368706%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Mme_Tussaud_museum_%282848368706%29.jpg/440px-Mme_Tussaud_museum_%282848368706%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mme_Tussaud_museum_(2848368706).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A wax sculpture of Caine in his <a href="/wiki/Harry_Palmer" title="Harry Palmer">Harry Palmer</a> character from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ipcress_File_(film)" title="The Ipcress File (film)">The Ipcress File</a></i>, at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a>, London</div></div></div>\n<p>The comedy sketch show, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Enfield%27s_Television_Programme" title="Harry Enfield&#39;s Television Programme">Harry Enfield\'s Television Programme</a></i>, included a series of sketches in which <a href="/wiki/Paul_Whitehouse" title="Paul Whitehouse">Paul Whitehouse</a> played a character called Michael Paine; an amalgam of previous Michael Caine impressions, who in a reference to Caine\'s character <a href="/wiki/Harry_Palmer" title="Harry Palmer">Harry Palmer</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ipcress_File" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ipcress File">The Ipcress File</a></i> wears oversized, thick-rimmed glasses and a trench coat. He introduces himself with the line, "My name is Michael Paine, and I am a nosy neighbour" and in a spoof of the stakeout at the beginning of <i>The Ipcress File</i>, recounts to the camera the \'suspiciously\' mundane behaviour of his neighbours, before saying, "Not a lot of people know that I know that".<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A parody of Caine appears in the animated series <i><a href="/wiki/Ugly_Americans_(TV_series)" title="Ugly Americans (TV series)">Ugly Americans</a></i>, in the episode "The Dork Knight", which also parodies the film <i>The Dark Knight</i>. In the episode, Caine appears as himself, portrayed in the light of his Alfred Pennyworth interpretation, and constantly annoys the protagonists with endless anecdotes of his career.\n</p><p>The 2010 television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Trip_(2010_TV_series)" title="The Trip (2010 TV series)">The Trip</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Rob_Brydon" title="Rob Brydon">Rob Brydon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Coogan" title="Steve Coogan">Steve Coogan</a>, featured improvised scenes in which the two leads argue over who can do the better Michael Caine impression.<sup id="cite_ref-Brydon_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brydon-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Among the lines they repeat in their attempts to outdo each other are, "You were only supposed to blow the bloody doors off!" and, "She was only sixteen"\xe2\x80\x94from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job" title="The Italian Job">The Italian Job</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Carter_(1971_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Get Carter (1971 film)">Get Carter</a></i>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Brydon_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brydon-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Coogan and Brydon later did their impressions from a balcony at the Royal Albert Hall during a celebration of Caine\'s work, only to be interrupted by the real Caine informing them that they were out of shape: "For me, it\'s a full-time job."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Craig_Ferguson" title="Craig Ferguson">Craig Ferguson</a> ran segments on his show where he parodied Caine, usually while wearing a <a href="/wiki/Space_suit" title="Space suit">space suit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In a 2010 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i>, Caine spoke of the impersonations and how everyone he meets quotes lines at him, to the point he quotes them quoting him.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> When asked did he ever tire of telling his anecdotes, Caine states: "I enjoy making people laugh. The trick is to tell them against yourself. If you praise yourself your stories aren\'t funny."<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg/170px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg" width="170" height="408" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg/255px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg/340px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="393" data-file-height="944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2008_Scarlett_Johansson_Michael_Caine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caine with <a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert" title="Nobel Peace Prize Concert">Nobel Peace Prize Concert</a>, December 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>Caine lives in <a href="/wiki/Leatherhead" title="Leatherhead">Leatherhead, Surrey</a>, in a house with a movie theatre which cost him \xc2\xa3100,000 to build.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He is patron to the Leatherhead Drama Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> He has also lived in <a href="/wiki/North_Stoke,_Oxfordshire" title="North Stoke, Oxfordshire">North Stoke, Oxfordshire</a>; <a href="/wiki/Clewer" title="Clewer">Clewer, Berkshire</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lowestoft" title="Lowestoft">Lowestoft, Suffolk</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Harbour" title="Chelsea Harbour">Chelsea Harbour, London</a>. In addition, Caine owns an apartment at the Apogee in <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="Miami Beach, Florida">Miami Beach, Florida</a>. He still keeps a small flat near where he grew up in London. Caine has published two volumes of memoirs, <i>What\'s It All About?</i> in 1992 and <i>The Elephant to Hollywood</i> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine was married to actress <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Haines" title="Patricia Haines">Patricia Haines</a> from 1955 to 1962. They have a daughter, Dominique (who was named after the heroine of the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fountainhead" title="The Fountainhead">The Fountainhead</a></i> by Ayn Rand).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He dated <a href="/wiki/Bianca_Jagger" title="Bianca Jagger">Bianca Jagger</a> in 1968. Caine has been married to actress and model <a href="/wiki/Shakira_Caine" title="Shakira Caine">Shakira Baksh</a> since 8 January 1973. They met after Caine saw her appearing in a <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_House" title="Maxwell House">Maxwell House</a> coffee commercial and a friend gave him her telephone number. He called her every day for ten days until she finally agreed to meet him.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> They have a daughter, Natasha Haleema.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> As a Christian married to a Muslim, he says "no questions or issues ever come up" and describes his wife\'s beliefs as "very benign".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Proud of his <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a> roots, Caine has discussed the opportunities his film career gave him: "I got to play football with <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pel\xc3\xa9">Pel\xc3\xa9</a>, for God\'s sake. And I danced with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Fosse" title="Bob Fosse">Bob Fosse</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> He also became close friends with <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, stating: "With John and I it was a case of bonding because we were both working class and we shared a sense of humour. We were pretending we weren\'t who people thought we were."<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> His closest friends include two James Bond actors, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> and the late <a href="/wiki/Roger_Moore" title="Roger Moore">Roger Moore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Caine quit his 80-a-day smoking habit in the early 1970s after a lecture by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Curtis" title="Tony Curtis">Tony Curtis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He is a fan of <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>. This was alluded to by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a>, who acted with Caine in the <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Knight_Rises" class="mw-redirect" title="Dark Knight Rises">Dark Knight Rises</a></i>, when he talked about Caine\'s acting methods: "It\'s, \'Take one\'. He got it. \'Take two\', got it. \'Take three\', got it. He\'s just on the money. [...] He doesn\'t fuck around because he wants to get back to cricket."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some time after his mother died, Caine and his younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Caine" title="Stanley Caine">Stanley</a>, learned they had an elder half-brother named David. He suffered from severe <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">epilepsy</a> and had been kept in <a href="/wiki/Cane_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Cane Hill">Cane Hill Mental Hospital</a> his entire life. Although their mother regularly visited her first son in the hospital, even her husband did not know the child existed. David died in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Trivia books written by Caine include <i>Not Many People Know That!</i>, <i>And Not Many People Know This Either!</i>, <i>Michael Caine\'s Moving Picture Show</i>, and <i>Not a Lot of People Know This is 1988</i>. Proceeds from the books went to the <a href="/wiki/National_Playing_Fields_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="National Playing Fields Association">National Playing Fields Association</a>, a UK charity for which Caine served as Vice President, and which aims to protect and promote open spaces for sports and recreation in British cities and towns.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, Caine changed his name by <a href="/wiki/Deed_poll" title="Deed poll">deed poll</a> to his long-time stage name in order to simplify security checks at airports. "[A security guard] would say, \'Hi Michael Caine,\' and suddenly I\'d be giving him a passport with a different name on it [Maurice Joseph Micklewhite]. I could stand there for an hour. So I changed my name."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_views">Political views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Caine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Political views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Caine has often been outspoken about his political views.
